"The trouble started with an inflamma
tion of the ear," said Dr. Chamberlain,
"and spread to the mastoid cells that are
beneath the bone, immediately behind
the ear. It was necessary to open these
in order to relieve the patient of the pos
sibility of the inflammation spreading to
the brain. There will . be danger from
complications until these cells are thor
oughly healed." .
Dr. Chamberlain, the attending physi
cian, said late to-night that Mrs. Booth-
Tucker was resting easily and that she
had rallied from the shock following the
operation. He expressed the opinion
that the chances of recovery were in
her favor.
Consul Tucker was first overtaken by Ill
ness just after her arrival on Saturday
last. She suffered- from a severe earache,
but did not think it necessary to consult a
physician until the pain became so great
that she could not stand it any longer.
Dr. Chamberlain, to whom she then went,
found that an absceSs was forming in the
ear. . He lanced the abscess at the home of
Colonel French in East Oakland, but lit
tle relief was afforded the patient. As she
continued to suffer Dr. Chamberlain ad
vised her to submit t6 an operation.
So serious is Consul Tucker's health that
her husband has been sent for and he is
now on his way from the headquarters of
the Salvation Army in New York.
.While the operation was successful and
the doctors are hopeful, the strain on the
sick woman's health has been very great
and she is now in a much weakened con
dition. She is not deemed in robust health
under ordinary circumstances and her
condition is such now that the slightest
change one way or another means life or
death.
Consul Booth-Tucker of tne Salvation
Army lies critically ill at the Fabiola Hos
pital as a result of an operation that was
performed for an abscess of the ear. Dr.
N. H. Chamberlain, assisted by other phy
sicians, treated the patient this morning
at the hospital by making an incision back
of -the affected ear and removing the ob
struction that has been causing her to suf
fer the most excruciating pain since her
arrival in Oakland last Saturday.

The suit in the Supreme Court may be
immediately followed by an action along
the same lines in the Supreme Court of
New Jersey.
The Attorney General will leave to
morrow night for Washington and will
institute the State's suit Monday in the
Federal Supreme Court. His appearance
ilonday will be a formality. The court
will set a date for the hearing and Doug
las will return to Minnesota. When he
next goes to Washington he will be ac
companied by George P. Wilson and L. S.
Munn, his associates in the case. Then
the great battle will be on in earnest.
The institution of the tirst suit m the
United States Supreme Court is in line
with the original plan made by Douglas.
Regardless oi its erfect on the ultimate re
sult of the right, it will definitely settle
the question of jurisdiction, which is
somewhat clouded.
MINNEAPOLIS, Jan- 2.â Governor Van
Sant and Attorney General Douglas
reached home this afternoon. Both drove
straight to the Capitol and went to work
on the railway merger cafe. ' / ' : .
The negro Cornelius was in the cab as
sisting the inspector, John McDonald, who
was on top of the engine. They were
blown to atoms. The others were at some
distance from the engine. It is supposed
that the negro had found the water in
the boiler too low and had suddenly in
jected a stream of cold water on the red
hot crownsheet. The engine was reduced
to .fragments, parts being -hurled through
the building two or three hundred yards.
One piece weighing 3000 pounds was
thrown 150 yards.

fracture, will die; R. L. Willis, black
smith, severely scalded; F. D. Hambrick,
carpenter, head lacerated; William Wil
son, carpenter, fractured ribs; J. M.
Meadows, carpenter, general bruises;

Wesley Johnson (colored), face cut;

just out of the shop and fired up. in the

McCUTCHEN
PARTY CAUSES
SPECULATION
It has been decided to take up Cuban
reciprocity immediately after Congress re
assembles next week. No bill has yet
been framed and the question will not
take this form until hearings have been
held and all shades of opinion expressed.
It is 'the intention of the committee to
have protracted hearings open to all peo
ple interested in the question of the
sugar and tobacco tariffs. The majority
of the Republican' members of the Way3
and -Means Committee are still opposed
to lowering the rates on Cuban products,
but the administration, represented in this
matter by Secretary Root, Is still insist
ing that something be done and done at
once for the alleged relief of , the people of
the island. Undoubtedly some sort of a bill
will be brought in, but just what form
it will take no one on the committee can
now predict. Senator Platt of Connecticut
had . a long conference with President
Roosevelt to-day on the Cuban situation.
Chairman Payne and Representatives
Dalzell and Long of the Ways and Means
Committee had a long conference to-day
on the question of the Cuban tariff and
other matters that will soon occupy the
attention of the House. '.

W., WASHINGTON, Jan. 2.â It is thought

to get into a deadlock on the Philippine

ers are In favor of scaling down the rates
on goods 1 coming from the Philippines to
this country and when the bill comes out
of the upper branch it is altogether prob
able that it- will be a different measure
from what it is now.
Special Dispatch to The Call.
Charles H. Scherrer, former Mayor of
Brooklyn, who was a delegate "of the
Chamber of Commerce to the reciprocity
convention at Washington, said he ob
jected to any reflection being cast upon
that convention. He eaid in part:
The men who composed that convention were
the very men -who were responsible for the
great prosperity of the country. We canno*
compete with foreign countries because of the
quality of poods we manufacture. So long as
wp have the Fystem of protection we can em
ploy skilled labor, which makes our poods
what they are. If the duty is taken off we
will have to cease employing the skilled me
chanics and employ the ordinary laborer and
when that is done the present high standard
of o-jr manufactures will be gone. You can
not adopt this report without casting a reflec
tion on that convention and on the country at
large.
The following substitute for the report
of the committee was offered, but was re
jected:
Resolved. That this body does not recom
mend reciprocity in our trade with foreign
countries until it can be done without injur
ing any of our own products and manufactures.
The committee report and resolutions
were then adopted.
Gustave H. Schwab, chairman of the
committee on foreign commerce, support
ed the resolutions, saying he thought the
injury which would be done to certain in
dustries by reciprocity was eo small com
rared to the great good which would re
sult to the country at large as to be not
worth considering.

' 6Â»rding e the valuable and beneficial work

the trade of these countries would be thrown
open to us; therefore, be it

ington on November ae subversive of all at

country to 1 the great detriment of its commer
cial interests.

;^ * COURT IS INCREASING

During the year 1901 the Supreme Court
decided 701 cases in which written opinions
were delivered. %'This is the largest num
ber of such cases decided for several
years. This number does not include the
vast number of decisions on motions, peti
tions for original writs, petitions for hear
ings in \bank: after decisions in department
and for rehearings after decisions in bank,
etc.". in "Which written opinions are not re-
Quired and I were not delivered. ;
During 1901 there were filed in the clerk's
office' C23 , -transcripts t on appeal, so that
the net gain for the year was seventy-nine
cases.' The general, business of 'the court
is behind in the San.- Francisco district' a
little less than two years; in' the Los An
geles district one year, and in the Sac
ramento district a little less than one
year. Thereforeif the gain for the last
year should be continued in the future the
court 'would be up "with its Â¦ business in
"the. next' two- or three years. It is be
lieved that the court is much more nearly
abreast its business than the average of
highest appellate courts of other States.
Lost Her Sealskin Coat.
A" S. J. -de Guerre of the firm of Arm
strong & De Guerre, who lives on Hart
ford street; reported to the police yester
day that his wife's 'sealskin coat, valued
at $200, . had been stolen while they were
partaking of "supper, at the Cafe Zinkand
bet-ween 11 and - 12 o'clock last 'Â¦ Tuesday
night.'. His wife .had placed her. coat on
the back of her chair, and after. supper
when she turned round to put j it on it
had disappeared. The cafe was crowded
at the .time- and' no one seemed' to have
noticed 'the 'theft. An' accurate descrip
tion of the coat was given and Captain
Seymour has detailed two detectives to
find ft if possible. ..

Generals Young, Kobbe and Randall
" Leave to Inspect Proposed Sites
in the South.-
Major General Young, : accompanied by
Generals j Randall and ' Kobbe, left for San
Diego yesterday morning for. the purpose
of selecting a suitable site for. one of the
four national camps which are to be used
for the drill of large bodies of troops.
Santa Barbara and Monterey have both
been mentioned as favorable locations for
the projected camp,; and an inspection of
these cities will be, made before the offi
cers return./ The report of the inspection
will .be presented to the War Department
about, the middle of the month. ;.

Call for Financial Statements
The Board of Bank Commissioners has
issued a call to all the banks in the State
to prepare a statement of their respective
resources and liabilities as they existed at
the close of the year. It is expected thtt
the reports will be' completed and pub
lished within the next two weeks

One Man Wounded in the Neck and
Three Bullets Fired Into a
Dwelling.
Two reports were made to the police
yesterday of wild and dangerous shoot
ing on New Year's eve or morning. Jo
. eeph Santa Cruz. 312 Andover street, re
ported that while he was on his way
home about midnight he was struck on
the neck by a bullet fired by an unknown
person at Cortland avenue and Benning
ton street. The bullet fortunately only in
flicted a slight flesh wound.
Michael CDea, 1126 Folson street, re
ported that shortly after midnight three
shots were fired at his house. One of the
bullets went through a rear window car
omed off the wall and landed on a table
in the room. The other two bullets went
through the side of the house. O'Dea
said he thouglit the shots were fired ma- i
liciously and that he had a strong sus
picion as to who fired them, but declined
to give any name.

Manager. Charles E. Cook of the Central
Theater- was called to. the stage New
Year's night to quell what was represent'
ed 'to be a small-sized riot, and when ho
responded to the summons he found he
was the central figure in a demonstration
in â¢ his favor. . Stage Manager George ' P.
Webster explained .. that " .the group of
actors, stage hands and . the entire ! force
of - theatrical ; employes t appreciated Mr.
Cook's services during the year and that
they felt some. little token of their appre
ciation, would not be- amiss. "With that
Georgie Cooper, began "For He's a. Jolly
Good Fellow," with the others following
in the chorus. Mr.; Cook was dumfound
ed'and especially so when the lights were
flashed up in the auditorium, revealing
an 1 , assemblage of â¢ nearly --one hundred
friends In the boxes and front seats of
the orchestra. Stage \ Manager Webster
then? relieved Mr. Cook of a handsome
gold watch that had been presented to him
a week . previously by Manager Fred
Belasco and appended to it a magnificent
chain, and locket. Manager Cook was at
a- loss to say -any thing and called upon
James Corrigan to help him' out, which
the latter laughingly refused to do." Then
at last mustering courage | the recipient
of the gift' thanked all - and a general
handshaking followed.

ANNOUNCEMENT.)
The Independent Gas and Power
Company announces that its new
and complete plant Is rapidly being
finished.
It has placed orders for about ten
â¢ thousand (10,000) tons of pipe, and
has on hand about two thousand
(2000) tons.
The laving of mains will com-
mence immediately after January
1st and be prosecuted as rapidly as
possible.
This company will make contracts
to supply gas for two years at the
rate of seventy-five {75) cents per
thousand cubic feet in all districts
as rapidly as the necessary pipes can
be laid.
